      - [Add a domain field to a table](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_AddADomainFieldToATable.md) -- As an administrator, domain-separate a custom table by adding a sys_domain field to it.
      - [View domain relationships](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_ViewDomainRelationships.md) -- The domain map offers domain administrators a read-only representation of the active domains on the instance and how they relate to each other.
        - [Select a primary domain](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_SelectAPrimaryDomain.md) -- The primary domain indicates the top-level domain in the domain map.
        - [Create Contains relationships between domains](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_CrContRelBetDom.md) -- Create a "contains" relationship between domains to change the domain hierarchy.
        - [Expand domain scope](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_ChangeDomainVisibility.md) -- By default, when a user in the global domain views a table containing a sys_overrides column, the user sees records from only the global domain. When an admin in the global domain views a process table, that admin sees only records that are in that process table.
          - [Add domains to a visibility domains list](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_AddADomainToAVisibilityDomainList.md) -- Adding a visibility domain allows a user or group to see and potentially edit records from another domain regardless of the user or group's normal domain membership.
          - [Grant visibility domains to an individual user](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_GrVisDomIndUser.md) -- While it is possible to add visibility domains for specific users on the User form, it's best to add them only via groups. This controls permissions and access should individuals change departments or leave the company.
      - [Create a domain-specific choice list](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_CreateADomainSpecificChoiceList.md) -- Administrators can configure choice lists to contain entries specific to a particular domain.
      - [Advanced administration](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/c_DomainSeparationAdministration.md) -- Administrators can view information about domain separation, identify potential issues, and change configuration settings.
        - [Use domain selection menus](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/c_DisplayingDomainSelectionMenus.md) -- The instance offers domain selection via two menu formats.
          - [Enable domain selection menus in Core UI](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_EnableDomainReferencePickerProperty.md) -- Displaying the domain picker in Core UI enables the domain selector by default. After enabling the domain selector, you can add a system property to enable the domain reference picker.
          - [Restrict access to the domain picker](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_RestrictAccesstoDomainPicker.md) -- Use a system property to restrict access to the domain picker in Core UI and Next Experience.
        - [Application properties](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ds-application-properties.md) -- The Domain Separation plugin has two new tables to give service providers more flexibility in customizing their applications that use domain separation. These tables are the System Application Property table [sys_application_property] and the System Application Property Value table [sys_application_property_value].
      - [Domain Migration Tool](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/tenant-domain-migration-tool.md) -- Use the Domain Migration Tool to move a customer from a domain-separated environment to their own dedicated instance.
        - [Migrate a domain-separated instance to a dedicated instance](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/tenant-domain-migration-tool.md) -- Use the Domain Migration Tool to move a customer from a domain-separated environment to their own dedicated instance.
      - [Process administration](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/c_DelegatedAdministration.md) -- Process administration allows administrators to set domain-specific policies.
        - [Example: Domain specific applications](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/r_ExDelAdmDomAppMod.md) -- The following example illustrates process administration with domain-specific applications and modules.
      - [Enable logging and debug messages](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_EnableDomainLogDebugMsgs.md) -- Domain log and debug messages allow you to troubleshoot domain configuration errors.
        - [View a real-time domain message](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_ViewARealTimeDomainMessage.md) -- You can view real-time domain messages from the system logs.
        - [View a historical domain message](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/t_ViewAHistoricalDomainMessage.md) -- View historical domain messages in the log file to troubleshoot domain separation issues.
        - [Troubleshoot domain separation errors](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/r_TroubleshootDomainSeparationError.md) -- If you encounter domain separation issues, review this list of solutions.
      - [Post-Production Domain Separation Activation Utility](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/post-prod-domain-sep-utility.md) -- The post-production Domain Separation activation utility aids in the activation of Domain Separation in a live environment.
      - [Domain Job Management](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/domain-job-manger.md) -- Queue multiple Domain Separation updates sequentially into a single background job using the Domain Job Manager.
      - [Delete by domain](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/delete-by-domain.md) -- Clean up inactive leaf level domains in the domain hierarchy with a controlled and automated tool.
    - [Domain Separation Center](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/domain-separation-center.md) -- Audit your domains regularly to reveal problems.
      - [Configure the Domain Separation Center](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/configure-the-domain-separation-center.md) -- Specify which tables in domains are large and whether you want detailed logging.
      - [Configure audits](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/configure-domain-separation-audits.md) -- Configure whether an audit is active and how frequently it runs.
      - [Schedule audits](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/schedule-audits.md) -- Specify the time and day that audits are run.
      - [Execute audits immediately](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/execute-audits-immediately.md) -- Audits typically run as scheduled. You can, however, run all audits on command.
      - [View audits with warnings and errors](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/view-audits-with-warnings-and-errors.md) -- The Domain Separation Center provides details about audit errors and warnings.
      - [View running and pending results](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/view-running-and-pending-results.md) -- You can view running and pending audits to see their status.
      - [View inactive audits](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/view-inactive-audits.md) -- You can view all inactive audits in one place and optionally activate them.
  - [Authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/c_Authentication.md) -- ServiceNow's authentication validates the identity of a user who accesses an instance, and then authorizes the user to features that match the user's role or job function.
    - [Adaptive authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-authentication.md) -- Use the Adaptive authentication policy framework to enforce contextual authentication controls to the right users at the right time. Adaptive authentication uses authentication policies to evaluate authentication requests and then either deny or allow access to your instance based on the specified policy conditions.
      - [Activate adaptive authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-authentication-plugin.md) -- You can activate the Adaptive Authentication plugin (com.snc.adaptive_authentication) for Adaptive Authentication if you have the admin role.
      - [Filter criteria](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-auth-filter-criteria.md) -- Filter criteria (also called policy inputs) are used as inputs for policy conditions to verify and meet the requirements of an authentication request.
        - [IP Filter](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/ip-filter.md) -- Use IP filter criteria to filter the users based on the user's IP addresses. Both IPv4 and IPv6 are supported.
          - [Create IP filter criteria](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-ip-filter-criteria.md) -- IP filter criteria allows you to filter users based on the user's IP addresses. You can configure an authentication policy to allow or deny access to a specific address or range of addresses.
        - [Role Filter](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/role-filter.md) -- Use role filter criteria to filter users based on their roles.
          - [Create role filter criteria](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-role-filter-criteria.md) -- Role filter criteria allows you to filter users based on the roles. You can configure an authentication policy to allow or deny access to a list of user roles.
        - [Group Filter](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/group-filter.md) -- Use group filter criteria to filter users based on the user group to which the user belongs.
          - [Create group filter criteria](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-group-filter-criteria.md) -- Group filter criteria allows or denies user access based on the user group to which the user belongs.
        - [Location Filter](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/location-filter.md) -- Location filter criteria can be used as filter input for users based on the user location.
          - [Activate Location Based Access](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-location-based-access.md) -- Activate the Zero Trust - Location Based Access (com.snc.zero_trust_location_access) to allow admins to configure adaptive authentication policies based on the location of the user.
          - [Create location filter criteria](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-location-filter-criteria.md) -- Use location filter criteria to filter input for users authentication based on the user location.
          - [Tutorial: Use Location Filter criteria](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-location-filter-criteria.md) -- Describes steps to use location filter criteria in the authentication policy and restrict access to the users based on the location.
            - [Use Location Filter in Pre Authentication Context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-lf-pre-auth.md) -- Use the location filter criteria created in the Pre Authentication Context.
            - [Use Location Filter Post Authentication Context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-lf-post-auth.md) -- Use the location filter criteria created in the Post Authentication Context.
            - [Use Location Filter in MFA Context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-lf-in-mfa.md) -- Use the location filter criteria created in MFA Context.
            - [Use Location Filter for Session Access](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/lf-for-session-access.md) -- Use the location filter criteria created in Session Access to reduce roles based on the location of the user.
        - [Identity Provider Attributes Filter](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/identity-provider-attributes.md) -- Use the Identity Provider attributes that are received from the Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML) response and OpenID Connect (OIDC) from the Identity Provider (IdP) as a filter criteria for authentication.
          - [Attributes for SAML](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/idp-attributes-saml.md) -- Use the Identity Provider attributes that are received from the Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML) response and OpenID Connect (OIDC) from the Identity Provider (IdP) as a filter criteria for authentication.
            - [Use as filter criteria for SAML](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-idp-filter-criteria.md) -- Use the Identity Provider (IDP) attribute from the Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML) response as a filter criteria for authentication policy.
          - [Attributes for OIDC](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/idp-attributes-oidc.md) -- Use the Identity Provider attributes that are received from the OpenID Connect (OIDC) from the Identity Provider (IdP) as a filter criteria for authentication.
            - [Use as filter criteria for OIDC](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-idp-filter-criteria-oidc.md) -- Use the Identity Provider (IDP) attribute from the OpenID Connect (OIDC) response as a filter criteria for authentication policy.
      - [Authentication policy contexts](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/auth-policy-contexts.md) -- Use authentication policy contexts to determine how and when your instance enforces authentication policies.
        - [Pre authentication context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/pre-auth-context.md) -- The pre authentication policy context defines how and when a policy is enforced during the login process. The policy used in this context executes before your users see a login screen.
        - [Post-authentication context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/post-auth-context.md) -- The Post Authentication policy context defines how and when a policy is enforced during the login process. The policy used in this context executes after your users see a login screen.
        - [MFA context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/mfa-auth-context.md) -- The Multi-factor Authentication (MFA) policy context uses a policy to define how and when MFA is enforced during the login process.
        - [Account recovery context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/account-recovery-context.md) -- The account recovery context uses a policy to define how and when the account recovery can be established.
        - [Session validation context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/session-context.md) -- Use the Session Validation Context as an additional layer of protection against session or cookie hijacking.
          - [Activate Session Validation Context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-session-validation-context.md) -- Use Session Validation Context to restrict access to ServiceNow when hijackers copy a user's session cookies from one device to another to impersonate the session or restricts the user's session access if they’re using an insecure network.
          - [Tutorial: Configuring session validation](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/use-ip-session-context.md) -- Configure session validation within the Adaptive Authentication framework to provide as an additional layer of protection for session or cookie hijacking.
      - [Authentication policies](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/authentication-policies.md) -- Authentication policies evaluate authentication requests based on the specified policy conditions and either allow or deny access depending on the output of policy conditions evaluation. For example, access is allowed only if all the policy conditions specified in Allow Access Policy evaluate to true.
        - [Configure a policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-allow-access-policy.md) -- Configure an authentication policy to define inputs and conditions to used to grant access to an instance or enforce multi-factor authentication.
        - [Add to an authentication policy context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/add-policy-to-context.md) -- Add an authentication policy to one of the authentication policy contexts. The authentication context uses the policy inputs and conditions to determine whether uses are granted access to the instance, or whether MFA is enforced for your users.
      - [Adaptive Authentication Events](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-authentication-events.md) -- You can use the adaptive authentication events table to know about the events.
      - [Configure properties](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-adaptive-auth-properties.md) -- After activating Adaptive Authentication, configure adaptive authentication properties according to your security requirements.
        - [Tutorial: Configure adaptive authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-auth-example.md) -- Use these example steps to configure adaptive authentication on an instance.
          - [Create a filter criteria record](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-auth-example.md) -- Use these example steps to configure adaptive authentication on an instance.
          - [Create a policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-auth-example.md) -- Use these example steps to configure adaptive authentication on an instance.
          - [Configure a policy context](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/adaptive-auth-example.md) -- Use these example steps to configure adaptive authentication on an instance.
      - [Adaptive Authentication for Trusted Mobile Apps](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/mobile-adaptive-authentication.md) -- Access your ServiceNow from untrusted networks by using the Now Mobile app.
        - [Activate Trusted Mobile App](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-trusted-mobile-app.md) -- Activate Adaptive Authentication with Trusted Mobile app by using the authentication policy and filter conditions.
        - [Register a trusted device](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/register-trusted-device.md) -- Register a trusted device to access the ServiceNow instance outside the network.
        - [Manage your trusted device](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/manage-your-trusted-device.md) -- Manage your trusted device from the Trusted Device registration page.
        - [Registration details of registered devices](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/device-app-registration-details.md) -- View the details of devices that are registered with your ServiceNow instance.
        - [Trusted Mobile App troubleshooting](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/troubleshooting-trusted-device.md) -- Review these troubleshooting scenarios to resolve issues with Trusted Mobile App.
    - [API authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/api-authentication.md) -- Authentication configurations for API.
      - [Certificate based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/certificate-api-auth.md) -- Certificate-based authentication lets you mutually authenticate inbound API requests using certificates from a trusted Certificate Authority (CA).
      - [OAuth](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/oauth-inbound-and-outbound.md) -- OAuth based authentication validates the identity of the client that attempts to establish a trust on the system by using an authentication protocol.
      - [Token-based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/token-based-auth-api.md) -- Token-based authentication for inbound REST APIs configuration using API Key or HMAC.
        - [API Key and HMAC Authentication for inbound REST APIs](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/api-key-and-hmac-rest-apis.md) -- Support API tokens for REST API endpoints so that the ServiceNow user name and password isn't visible in the webhook URL.
          - [Activate API Key and HMAC Authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/active-api-key-hmac.md) -- You can activate the plugin API Key and HMAC Authentication (com.glide.tokenbased_auth) in your ServiceNow instance.
          - [Configure API key - Token-based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-api-key.md) -- Configure an API key to support authentication for REST API endpoints.
          - [Configure HMAC - Token-based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-hmac.md) -- Configure HMAC to support authentication for REST API endpoints.
          - [Cleaning up token Expiry](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/token-expiry-api-and-hmac.md) -- Details about how to clean up token expiry by using different system properties.
      - [Basic authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/basic-authentication.md) -- Legacy API authentication method using username and password, with restricted usage and varying behaviour in zBoot and upgraded instances.
    - [API access policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/api-access-policy.md) -- API access policy defines the permissions and duration of access to an API.
      - [REST API access policies](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/inbound-authentication-profile.md) -- REST API access policies allow you to restrict access to inbound REST APIs based on the authentication type and the specified filter criteria of the access policy.
        - [Activate REST API access policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-rest-api-access-policy.md) -- You can activate the REST API Access Policy plugin (com.glide.rest.policy) if you have the admin role. If the application does NOT include demo data or it does NOT install related applications and plugins, delete or revise the following sentence:The application includes demo data and installs related ServiceNow Store applications and plugins if they are not already installed.
        - [Create an authentication profile](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-authentication-profile.md) -- Create an authentication profile and add one or more authentication policies to the profile. You can also configure the ID Token and OAuth Token authentication profiles that are available by default.
        - [Create REST API access policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-api-access-policy.md) -- Create an API access policy and map an authentication profile to restrict the authentication type for a REST API. For example, you can create an API access policy that allows only ID token authentication for a REST API.
          - [API access policy prioritization](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/api-access-policy-prioritization.md) -- Learn about the policy prioritization logic if there are multiple API access policy configured for your ServiceNow instance.
        - [REST API Auth Scope](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/rest-api-auth-scope.md) -- Use the REST API Auth Scope to provide access to a specific REST API
          - [Activate REST API Auth Scope](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-rest-api-auth-scope.md) -- You can activate the REST API Auth Scope plugin (com.glide.rest.auth.scope) to link the OAuth entity with authentication scopes.
          - [Properties and tables](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/rest-api-auth_scope-properties.md) -- The REST API Auth Scope plugin (com.glide.rest.auth.scope) includes the following system properties, tables, and scripts.
          - [Configure auth scope](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-rest-api-auth-scope.md) -- Link the OAuth entity with an auth scope to manage the token to access the REST APIs that are linked with the auth scope.
          - [Troubleshooting](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/rest-api-scope-troubleshooting.md) -- Troubleshooting actions can help resolve common issues when setting up or running the REST API scope.
      - [SOAP API access policies](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/soap-api-access-policies.md) -- SOAP API access policies allow you to restrict access to inbound SOAP APIs based on the authentication type and the specified filter criteria of the access policy.
        - [Activate SOAP API access policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-soap-api-access-policy.md) -- For SOAP API access policy, install the SOAP API Access Policy (com.glide.soap.policy) plugin.
        - [Create an authentication profile](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-an-authentication-profile.md) -- Create an authentication profile and add one or more authentication policies to the profile. You can also configure the ID Token and OAuth Token authentication profiles that are available by default.
        - [Create SOAP API access policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-soap-api-access-policy.md) -- Create an API access policy and map an authentication profile to restrict the authentication type for a SOAP API. For example, you can create an API access policy that allows only ID token authentication for a SOAP API.
          - [Create a global API access policy to protect SOAP APIs](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-global-api-access-protect-soap.md) -- Create a single global API access policy to protect all the SOAP APIs.
        - [Filter criteria for APIs](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/filter-criteria-apis.md) -- Filter criteria contains filter conditions or queries that are used as policy inputs for an authentication policy. Policy inputs are used to group one or more filter criteria and define the policy conditions of an authentication policy. For example, an IP Filter Criteria define an IP address in the Classless Inter-Domain Routing (CIDR) format or a range of IP addresses.
      - [API Authentication Policies](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/api-authentication-policies.md) -- Authentication policies evaluate authentication requests based on the specified policy conditions and either allows or denies access depending on the matching criteria.
        - [Create a policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-api-authentication-policy.md) -- Authentication policies allow you to enforce access restrictions on the APIs based on the specified filter criteria.
        - [Configure global blocking policy for APIs](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-global-blocking-policy-apis.md) -- Global blocking policy denies the authentication requests of users and APIs based on the specified policy conditions. This policy can be used as an alternative to the IP Address Access Control.
      - [System or Export Processors](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/api-auth-policy-export-processors.md) -- Ability for System or Export Processors to leverage processor access policy to secure all the export endpoints.
        - [Activate Processor access policy](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-processor-access-policy.md) -- For Processor, install the Processor Access policy (com.glide.processor.policy) plugin.
        - [Configure an Authentication profile](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-auth-profile-processor.md) -- Apply authentication profile for the export processors.
    - [Authentication factors](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/authentication-factors.md) -- Authentication factors help identify and verify callers, allowing only authorized users to access AI voice agents on the ServiceNow AI Platform.
      - [Explore authentication factors for AI voice agents](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/explore-authentication-factors.md) -- Authentication factors are the elements used for caller identification and authentication. In secure voice agent environments, the process begins with identifying the caller, followed by authenticating their identity before granting access. A robust security strategy combines multiple factors to confirm that only authorized users interact with AI voice agents.
      - [Configure authentication factors for AI voice agents](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configuring-authentication-factors-for-ai-voice-agents.md) -- To secure voice agent environments, configure authentication factors that first identify the caller, then authenticate them before granting access.
        - [Configure voice input for authentication factors](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-voice-authentication-factors.md) -- Configure how callers provide authentication responses by speaking or using the phone keypad.
        - [TOTP authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/totp-authenticator-apps.md) -- A time based one-time password (TOTP) is a secure authentication factor that verifies user identity by generating a unique, time-sensitive code.
        - [Push notification - Okta verify](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/push-notification-okta-verify.md) -- The Okta Verify app push notification enables users to securely approve authentication requests directly on their enrolled mobile devices.
          - [Configure push notification (Okta Verify)](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-okta-verify-push-notification.md) -- Configure Okta Verify to receive push notifications for secure and convenient identity verification.
        - [Soft PIN authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/softpin-authentication.md) -- Soft PIN is a six-digit numeric PIN that verifies a caller's identity during an AI voice agent session.
          - [Configure Soft PIN](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-soft-pin.md) -- Users are required to configure Soft PIN before it can be used for authentication with ServiceNow AI Platform.
        - [SMS OTP authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/sms-otp-authentication.md) -- SMS one-time password (OTP) authentication is a method used to verify user identity by sending a temporary, numeric code to the user's registered mobile number. The user enters this code to complete authentication.
        - [Email OTP authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/email-otp-authentication.md) -- Email OTP for AI voice agents sends a one-time numeric code to the caller's email address. The caller retrieves the code from their email and provides it to the agent to verify their identity.
          - [Configure Email OTP](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-email-otp-service.md) -- Configure the Email one-time password (OTP) to enable OTP-based authentication for users in your instance.
        - [Knowledge-based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/knowledge-based-authentication.md) -- Knowledge-based authentication (KBA) is an identification and authentication method that verifies callers by prompting them to answer preconfigured questions across conversational AI channels, such as AI voice agents. KBA can be used to identify a caller, authenticate a caller, or both within the same interaction.
          - [Configure KBA](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-kba.md) -- Configure knowledge-based authentication (KBA) to identify and authenticate callers by prompting them to answer preconfigured questions across conversational AI channels, such as AI voice agents.
            - [Create KBA questions](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-knowledge-based-questions.md) -- Create knowledge-based questions to use for caller identification and authentication in AI voice agent interactions.
            - [Create KBA answers](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-knowledge-based-answers.md) -- Create knowledge-based answers for the preconfigured security questions to confirm the user's identity.
            - [Map KBA questions to answers](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-kba-answer-mappings.md) -- Create knowledge-based questions and answer mapping to confirm the user's identity.
            - [AI voice agent service mapping with KBA](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/create-kba-service-mappings.md) -- Specify the questions used for caller identification and authentication with a specific AI voice agent service.
    - [Certificate-based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/certificate-based-authentication.md) -- Certificate-based authentication lets you mutually authenticate user logins or inbound API requests using certificates from a trusted Certificate Authority (CA).
      - [Set up](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/set-up-mutual-auth.md) -- Set up mutual authentication for either user interface-based logins or inbound web services.
        - [Activate Certificate-based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/set-up-mutual-auth.md) -- Set up mutual authentication for either user interface-based logins or inbound web services.
        - [Register CA certificate](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/set-up-mutual-auth.md) -- Set up mutual authentication for either user interface-based logins or inbound web services.
        - [Map PEM certificate to user](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/set-up-mutual-auth.md) -- Set up mutual authentication for either user interface-based logins or inbound web services.
        - [Configure Certificate-based authentication properties](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/set-up-mutual-auth.md) -- Set up mutual authentication for either user interface-based logins or inbound web services.
      - [Log in](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/ui-login-mutual-auth.md) -- After your administrator sets up Certificate-based authentication, you can register the client certificate and log in using your PIV (Personal Identity Verification) or CAC (Common Access Card) card.
        - [Register client certificate for your PIV or CAC card](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/ui-login-mutual-auth.md) -- After your administrator sets up Certificate-based authentication, you can register the client certificate and log in using your PIV (Personal Identity Verification) or CAC (Common Access Card) card.
        - [Log in to ServiceNow AI Platform using PIV or CAC card](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/ui-login-mutual-auth.md) -- After your administrator sets up Certificate-based authentication, you can register the client certificate and log in using your PIV (Personal Identity Verification) or CAC (Common Access Card) card.
        - [Manage your client certificates](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/certificate-based-authentication/ui-login-mutual-auth.md) -- After your administrator sets up Certificate-based authentication, you can register the client certificate and log in using your PIV (Personal Identity Verification) or CAC (Common Access Card) card.
    - [Custom instance URLs](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/custom-url.md) -- You can enable your ServiceNow instance to be accessible from a company-branded or custom URL.
      - [Activate custom URLs](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/activate-custom-url-plugin.md) -- Enable custom URLs to be set up on your ServiceNow instance. You can activate the Custom URL plugin (com.snc.customurl) if you have the admin role.
      - [Set as the instance URL](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/configure-custom-url.md) -- Add a custom URL to your instance configuration to use instead of your ServiceNow URL.
      - [Identity Provider](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/custom-url-with-multiple-identity-providers.md) -- Set your custom URL with the Identity Provider to enable the user to login with their IdP's.
      - [Datacenter job information](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/view-custom-url-datacenter-jobs.md) -- Every custom URL that is associated to your instance has a corresponding ServiceNow datacenter job which runs and shows URL information that is pertinent to your instance as described in the table.
      - [Generate SP metadata for SAML/SSO](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/generate-idp-metadata-sso.md) -- A SAML or SSO installation needs the SP metadata generated for the IdP before the custom URL instance generates.
      - [Custom URL errors and fixes](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/custom-url-error-fix.md) -- A list of common errors and associated fixes for a custom URL setup and configuration.Target Audience: ServiceNow Admin
    - [Installation exits](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/r_InstallationExits.md) -- Installation exits are customizations that exit from Java to call a script before returning back to Java.
    - [IP range based authentication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/c_IPRangeBasedAuthentication.md) -- One way to secure a web-based application is to restrict access based on the IP address.
      - [IP Address Access Control](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/t_AccessControl.md) -- Apply an IP access control to outbound traffic, inbound traffic, or bidirectional traffic. The system only blocks an IP address if a matching Deny rule exists and no matching Allow rule exists. By default, there are no restrictions on access to your instance.
      - [Find denied IP addresses](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/t_FindDeniedIPAddresses.md) -- Find Denied IP addresses in the instance's node log files.
    - [LDAP integration](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPIntegration.md) -- An LDAP integration allows your instance to use your existing LDAP server as the primary source of user data.
      - [Understand LDAP integration](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPIntegrationFAQs.md) -- An LDAP integration allows your instance to use your existing LDAP server as the primary source of user data.
      - [LDAP integration requirements](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPIntegrationRequirements.md) -- Review the requirements for LDAP integration, which include a PKI certificate an LDAP compliant directory services server.
      - [LDAP integration setup](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPIntegrationSetup.md) -- Administrators can enable LDAP integration to allow sign-on of users from their company LDAP directory.
        - [Install the LDAP X.509 SSL certificate](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_UploadTheX509SSLCertificate.md) -- You can install an X.509 certificate for your LDAP integration.
        - [Define an LDAP server](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_DefineAnLDAPServer.md) -- Create a new LDAP server record in the instance.
        - [Enable an LDAP listener and set system properties](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_EnableAListener.md) -- Enabling a listener is optional. If enabled, a listener notifies the system to process LDAP records soon after there is an update on the LDAP server.
        - [Specify the LDAP attributes](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_SpecifyLDAPAttributes.md) -- Specify the attributes included in LDAP server queries by using the LDAP server Attributes field. This can enhance performance as well as security.
        - [Test an LDAP connection](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_TestAnLDAPConnectionManually.md) -- The instance tests the connection automatically every time a user opens the LDAP Server form. Alternatively, you can manually test the connection to the LDAP server from the LDAP server form.
        - [Define LDAP organizational units](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_DefineLDAPOrganizationalUnits.md) -- An organizational unit (OU) definition specifies the LDAP source directories available to the integration.
        - [Create a data source for LDAP](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_CreateADataSource.md) -- Each LDAP organizational unit (OU) definition has its own related list of data sources.
        - [Auto provision LDAP users](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_AutoProvisionLDAPUsers.md) -- You automatically provision users who are in the LDAP server but not yet in your instance.
        - [LDAP integration via MID Server](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPIntegrationViaMIDServer.md) -- Administrators can integrate using an LDAP data source over a Management, Instrumentation, and Discovery (MID) Server.
          - [Configure LDAP connection monitoring](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ConfigureLDAPConnectionMonitoring.md) -- Change or disable LDAP connection monitoring and notifications.
          - [Import binary data through a MID Server](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ImportBinaryDataThroughAMIDServer.md) -- As an administrator, you can import binary large object (BLOB) data with an LDAP integration through the MID Server.
          - [Troubleshooting LDAP integration via MID Server](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_TroubleshootLDAPIntegViaMIDSvr.md) -- You may encounter issues in the following areas while integrating LDAP via MID Server.
      - [Import and map data](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPImportMaps.md) -- LDAP import maps match fields in your LDAP database to fields in your instance.
        - [LDAP transform maps](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPTransformMaps.md) -- The transform map moves data from the import set table to the target table (User or Group).
        - [LDAP scripting](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_CommonLDAPScripts.md) -- Create custom transform maps, scripts, and business rules to specify requirements when importing data.
          - [Set disabled Active Directory users to inactive](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_CommonLDAPScripts.md) -- Create custom transform maps, scripts, and business rules to specify requirements when importing data.
          - [Assign LDAP field values](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_CommonLDAPScripts.md) -- Create custom transform maps, scripts, and business rules to specify requirements when importing data.
          - [Exclude particular LDAP users](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_CommonLDAPScripts.md) -- Create custom transform maps, scripts, and business rules to specify requirements when importing data.
        - [Set choice action for reference field imports](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_SetChoiceAction.md) -- The LDAP transform map determines how fields in the Import Set table map to fields in existing tables such as Incident or User.
        - [Verify LDAP mapping](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_VerifyLDAPMapping.md) -- After creating an LDAP transform map, refresh the LDAP data to verify the transform map works as expected.
      - [LDAP integration troubleshooting](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPIntegrationTroubleshooting.md) -- If you are integrating your LDAP server and have questions, these items may help you troubleshoot the issue.
        - [View the LDAP monitor](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ViewLDAPMonitor.md) -- You can view current information about LDAP servers and listeners using LDAP monitor.
        - [LDAP error codes](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPErrorCodes.md) -- The LDAP Log file lists industry standard error codes for both LDAP and Active Directory (AD).
        - [Send a one-time password when the LDAP server is down](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_SendOneTimePassword.md) -- An LDAP property is available to send a one-time password to a user if the user is unable to log in because the LDAP server is down. You can also configure another property to control how long the password is valid.
      - [LDAP record synchronization](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_LDAPRecordSynchronization.md) -- Administrators can synchronize inactive, disabled, or deleted LDAP records with their LDAP records.
        - [LDAP refresh filters](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPRefreshFilters.md) -- Filters on the LDAP refresh process can be used to specify processing that ignores inserts of disabled users.
        - [LDAP extraction](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPExtraction.md) -- Implement an LDAP extraction process to detect inactive users.
        - [Inactive LDAP user accounts](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_InactiveLDAPUserAccounts.md) -- Detect that an existing, current, user account is inactive or has been disabled or deleted from an Active Directory (AD) LDAP.
          - [Use the userAccountControl field](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_FindInactLDAPAcctsWUsrAcctCtrlFld.md) -- Identify when an Active Directory (AD) user is deleted (or made inactive).
        - [LDAP script examples](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPScriptExamples.md) -- The following script examples assume you use an Active Directory (AD) for your LDAP server.
      - [Active Directory Application Mode (ADAM)](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_ActiveDirectoryApplicationMode.md) -- Active Directory Application Mode (ADAM) is an Lightweight Directory Access Protocol (LDAP)-compliant directory service.
        - [Configuring an instance](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ConfiguringAnInstance.md) -- The first install copies the ADAM files to your computer, registers requires components, and creates the application shortcuts.
        - [Set up the ADAM console](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_SettingUpTheConsole.md) -- Set up the ADAM console. Even though there are many similarities between ADAM and Active Directory, the administration can be very different since there is no Users and Computers management console.
        - [Create containers and organizational units](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_CreateContainersAndOrgUnits.md) -- Logically group objects stored in ADAM into containers and organizational units (OU) just as they would be in Active Directory.
        - [Delegation with ADAM](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_Delegation.md) -- Once the OU structure is created, define the permission delegations to properly secure the objects to limited users.
        - [Populating ADAM Objects](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_PopulatingADAMObjects.md) -- ADAM Objects include User Objects, UserProxy Object, and Group Objects.
        - [Testing and troubleshooting](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_TestingAndTroubleshooting.md) -- The primary tool used for testing is LDP. This allows you to fully test user authentication.
        - [Backup and recovery](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_BackupAndRecovery.md) -- All ADAM data can be backed up using standard file system backup methods.
        - [Use LDAPS with ADAM](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_UsingLDAPSWithADAM.md) -- The default configuration for userProxy object authentication is to enforce LDAPS (secure LDAP) communications. LDAPS requires SSL certificates to secure the network traffic.
          - [Assign the certificate to ADAM](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_AssigningTheCertificateToADAM.md) -- Install an SSL certificate on the server and any LDAP client to support secure binds and encrypt the user and password information being transmitted.
          - [Export the public key certificate](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ExportingThePublicKeyCertificate.md) -- LDAPS clients, including the instance need the public key certificate in order to make a secure connection to ADAM.
        - [ADAM access account](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_ServiceNowITSASuiteAccessAccount.md) -- The system requires a user account to read the Active Directory Application Mode (ADAM) object information that is imported into the application instance.
        - [Test the LDAPS connections](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_TestingLDAPSConnections.md) -- Test the LDAPS connections. There are two console connections, one for Local Computer Certificates, and the other for Local Computer Services Certificates on the new ADAM service.
        - [Use ADAMSync to populate ADAM](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_UsingADAMSyncToPopulateADAM.md) -- Administrators use MS ADAMSync to populate LDAP directories that use MS ADAM.
          - [Define ADAM user accounts](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_DefineUserAccounts.md) -- Define user accounts in ADAM. One user account is used for the instance to connect with and the other user account is for ADAMSync.
          - [Set up ADAMSync](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_SetUpADAMSync.md) -- ADAMSync is included with Windows Server 2003 R2. Download and install ADAMSync if you are using a different OS.
          - [Install the ADAM configuration file](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_InstallTheConfigurationFile.md) -- Install the ADAM configuration file through the Windows command line.
            - [Example ADAM configuration files](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_ExampleConfigurationFiles.md) -- All of the configurations for ADAMSync are stored in xml files.
      - [Configure Microsoft AD for secure LDAPS communication](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_ConfigureMicrosoftADForSSLAccess.md) -- Use certificate pairs to enable Microsoft Active Directory (AD) LDAPS communications.
        - [Set up a stand-alone certificate authority](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_SetUpAStandaloneCA.md) -- The first step to configure Microsoft Active Directory for SSL access is to set up a stand-alone Certificate Authority (CA).
        - [Generate a certificate from an internal certificate authority](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_GenACertificateFromAnInternalCA.md) -- When you configure Microsoft Active Directory for SSL access, you must generate an internal certificate and request the external certificate.
        - [Test the LDAPS connectivity locally](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_TesttheLDAPSConnectivityLocally.md) -- Test the LDAPS connectivity after installing the internal and third party certificates when you configure Microsoft Active Directory for SSL access.
        - [Export the public key certificate to trust the LDAP certificate](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ExportThePublicKeyCertificate.md) -- Export the public key certificate and import it into the application when you configure Microsoft Active Directory for SSL access.
      - [LDAP global catalog usage](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_LDAPUsingGlobalCatalog.md) -- A DC can be granted the Global Catalog (GC) role. Global Catalog (GC) role is an LDAP-compliant directory consisting of a partial representation of every object from every domain within a forest.
      - [OpenLDAP minor schema modification](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/r_OpenLDAPMinorSchemaModification.md) -- In OpenLDAP 2.3 systems that use the back-bdb (Berkley backend), administrators make a minor modification to their schema to facilitate the integration.
        - [Modify the schema](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/t_ModifyTheOpenLDAPSchema.md) -- Modify the OpenLDAP schema. These steps detail a schema modification to OpenLDAP 2.3 provided by one of our customers that helped them integrate with their instance.
      - [Record LDAP deletions](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/ldap-integration/c_DeletedRecords.md) -- By default, the instance does not delete any entries after they disappear from LDAP.
    - [Limit concurrent sessions](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/limit-concurrent-sessions.md) -- You can limit the number of concurrent interactive sessions for a user or role on an instance across all nodes.
      - [Explore limit concurrent sessions](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/explore-lcs.md) -- You can limit the number of concurrent interactive sessions for a user or role on an instance across all nodes.
      - [Configure the plugin](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/limit-concurrent-sessions-plugin.md) -- You can activate the Limit Concurrent Sessions plugin (com.glide.limit.concurrent.sessions) if you have the admin role.
      - [Set a limit by user or role](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/set-session-limit-user-role.md) -- You can set a concurrent session limit on a specific user or on a particular role.
      - [Disable a limit by user or role](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/disable-session-limit-user-role.md) -- You can disable a concurrent session limit on a specific user or on a particular role.

      - [Remember me](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/c_ChSetRemMeChkbxCookie.md) -- When the Remember me check box is selected at login, a cookie is stored on the user's computer. This cookie automatically authenticates the user upon subsequent visits.
        - [Change the default value of the Remember me check box](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/c_ChSetRemMeChkbxCookie.md) -- When the Remember me check box is selected at login, a cookie is stored on the user's computer. This cookie automatically authenticates the user upon subsequent visits.

    - [Multi-Provider single sign-on (SSO)](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/c_MultipleProviderSingleSignOn.md) -- External SSO allows organizations to use several SSO identity providers (IdPs) to manage authentication as well as retain local database (basic) authentication.

      - [Multi-Provider SSO configurations](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/sso-configurations.md) -- You must perform several steps to set up Multi-Provider SSO, including configuring properties, creating identity providers (IdPs), and configuring users to use SSO.

        - [Configure users for Multi-Provider SSO](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/t_ConfigureUsersMultiProviderSSO.md) -- Administrators can configure Multi-Provider SSO for individual users or for all users who belong to a company. You cannot configure Multi-Provider SSO for groups.
        - [Test IdP connections](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/t_TestIdPConnections.md) -- Testing the connection to an IdP validates the settings before enabling external authentication.
          - [Common IdP connection errors](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/r_CommonConnectionErrors.md) -- The following table describes some of the common IdP connection errors and their solutions.
          - [Troubleshoot script issues with SAML](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ServiceNow/ServiceNowDocs/zurich/markdown/platform-security/authentication/t_TroubleshootScriptIssuesWithSAML.md) -- Troubleshoot script issues with SAML. You might encounter script issues if SAML is already active at the time that you activate Multiple Single Sign-On and if you already customized the installation exits.
